<div id="review_1750452458" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1750452458" />
    <a title="Linda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4626387-linda"><img alt="Linda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1418713075p2/4626387.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1750452458?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Linda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Linda" href="/user/show/4626387-linda">Linda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1750452458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13214093986890647875">This rating is actually for the entire series. Iggulden has written a five-book series on the rise of the Mongols from Ghengis to Kublai Khan and it should be read in the order he wrote them for the history to sink in and make sense. It’s a great read!<br/><br/>Ghengis Khan brought the many different tribes of Mongols together to create the Mongol nation. He did it in spite of the fact that his family had been left to die when his father, the Khan of one of the tribes, died and another was chosen. He, his</span>
  <span id="freeText13214093986890647875" style="display:none">This rating is actually for the entire series. Iggulden has written a five-book series on the rise of the Mongols from Ghengis to Kublai Khan and it should be read in the order he wrote them for the history to sink in and make sense. It’s a great read!<br /><br />Ghengis Khan brought the many different tribes of Mongols together to create the Mongol nation. He did it in spite of the fact that his family had been left to die when his father, the Khan of one of the tribes, died and another was chosen. He, his mother, his four brothers and his infant sister hid in the mountains and managed to survive.<br /><br />Ghengis not only united the Mongols into one nation but he also destroyed the Chin dynasty of what is today northern China. Then he swung to the west and conquered much of the Muslim civilization. By the time he died, the Mongols had most of Middle Asia in their grasp.<br />Ghengis was a conqueror only. He had no intention of creating a nation with an infrastructure or settled government. He created a massive army and knew that, if not kept busy, it was likely to turn on him. He ruled by complete loyalty of his armies and complete terror of the subject nations. <br />He chose his third son as his successor. Odegai believed in a settled government and created a capital city. During this time there were no raids, but as soon as the city was completed, the Mongols began raiding again. Again terror ruled the countries.<br /><br />The next couple of changes of khan are more difficult to explain, so I’ll let you read about them. Kublai, the third son of the fourth son of Ghengis, was raised as a scholar. A young Buddhist monk had attached himself to the Mongols during the time of Ghengis and was chosen to instruct the sons. But Kublai’s brother who became Khan wanted a warrior brother and gave him an army and sent him to overcome the Sung dynasty - southern China. Amazingly, Kublai turned into a fabulous leader and was given China as his own Khanate. He established a capital at, you know, Xanadu but there was no pleasure palace – just a deer park.<br /><br />Watching the history progress, you can’t help but admire the Mongols. Iggulden does not gloss over their brutality and makes no excuses. But you begin to see the West in a different light. It’s a bit like watching the later Western armies fight against guerillas. A whole new type of warfare.<br />Do read the series. Iggulden’s style is very easy to read. You’re done with the book before you realize it. The history is fascinating, the characters incredible and the writing great. What’s to lose?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13214093986890647875" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_241452174" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/241452174" />
    <a title="Nancy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/108416-nancy"><img alt="Nancy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351512283p2/108416.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/241452174?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/108416-nancy">Nancy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385343053" href="/book/show/11526977-conqueror">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/108416-nancy?shelf=first-reads">first-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/108416-nancy?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer241452174" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15506456564415490082">This dramatic historical saga about the coming of age (and triumphs) of Kublai Khan took me out of my literary comfort zone and into a bold, brutal, and fascinating period of history.<br/><br/>I'm shamefully ignorant about Asian history and this book provided me with a background on the development of the Mongul empire. Iggulden did a stunning job in his profile of Kublai Khan. The transformation of an elegant young scholar into a fierce Mongol warrier seems unlikely at first, but the author made it seaml</span>
  <span id="freeText15506456564415490082" style="display:none">This dramatic historical saga about the coming of age (and triumphs) of Kublai Khan took me out of my literary comfort zone and into a bold, brutal, and fascinating period of history.<br /><br />I'm shamefully ignorant about Asian history and this book provided me with a background on the development of the Mongul empire. Iggulden did a stunning job in his profile of Kublai Khan. The transformation of an elegant young scholar into a fierce Mongol warrier seems unlikely at first, but the author made it seamless and believable. His portrait of The Conqueror was fascinating and I am grateful to the FirstReads program for giving me the opportunity to preview this book. It was a stretch for me to spend 460 pages reading about death and destruction, but it was also 460 pages of illumination about a brave people and a fascinating culture. <br /><br />Perhaps my greatest "ah-ha moment" was how Iggulden's story illuminated the challenge the western world is facing in its military engagements in the Middle East. The Mongul warriors spent years "on the road" just to reach their enemy's turf so they could engage in war. Years! Life was battle after battle after battle. Our expected timeframe for military action is a blade of grass on the landscape seen by the warriors of the cultures we are currently engaging. Their battles go on for generations and we expect something parallel to instant gratification. That was my takeaway--certainly I was aware of the vast cultural differences of the west and the east, but this book put it into an historical context for me.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15506456564415490082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_306201165" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/306201165" />
    <a title="Grady" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8034370-grady"><img alt="Grady" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1375016989p2/8034370.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/306201165?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Grady" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Grady" href="/user/show/8034370-grady">Grady</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer306201165" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8780842518803011381">It's a telenovela! for men! with Mongols! And, to be fair, it doesn't have many exclamation points, just a lot of brutal men living by a code of honor in a brutal era. Will Kublai, grandson of Genghis and second son of Tolui, outlive his gay cousin? his brutal older brother? his self-indulgent younger brother? Will he have more success in China than his other brother has against Bagdad and the Assassins? How many ways are there to depict weak men dying pathetically, crushed by fate? Overall, it'</span>
  <span id="freeText8780842518803011381" style="display:none">It's a telenovela! for men! with Mongols! And, to be fair, it doesn't have many exclamation points, just a lot of brutal men living by a code of honor in a brutal era. Will Kublai, grandson of Genghis and second son of Tolui, outlive his gay cousin? his brutal older brother? his self-indulgent younger brother? Will he have more success in China than his other brother has against Bagdad and the Assassins? How many ways are there to depict weak men dying pathetically, crushed by fate? Overall, it's a fine historical adventure, but (1) it seems surprisingly long for having so little actually happen in the plot; (2) Kublai Khan, who we're told is very smart, doesn't seem as sharp or brave as his top commanders -- he comes across as a bit of a whiner, really; and (3) perhaps to make the brutality more palatable to a soft modern audience, the losers are always meaner or more debauched than the winners, as though what happens to them is a kind of rough justice. But then, it's supposed to be satisfying fiction, so why not. And the cover certainly has a lot of Mongols on it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8780842518803011381" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6mO6vVhgMV/J8WPrZQSvYpWuCRp4UMS3r9A0JZr+nJNAJAWIqcrX5DKBmk5vCuWWNaCTHTIDbSGhB/xjpsNcig==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

As the sultan’s son schemes against his own family, old scars of the Crusades are quickly uncovered and new wounds appear. It was fought by two badly matched armies that met in atrocious conditions on St Crispin\'s Day 1415, and resulted in an extraordinary victory that was celebrated in England long before Shakespeare immortalised it in Henry V. It has always been held to be the triumph of the longbow against the armoured knight, and of the common man against the feudal aristocrat, but those are history\'s myths. Bernard Cornwell, who has long wanted to write this story, depicts the reality behind the myths.\n\nNicholas Hook is an English archer. He seems born to trouble and, when his lord orders him to London as part of a force sent to quell an expected Lollard uprising, Nick\'s headstrong behaviour leads to him being proscribed an outlaw. He finds refuge across the Channel, part of an English mercenary force protecting the town of Soissons against the French. What happened at the Siege of Soissons shocked all Europe, and propels Nick back to England where he is enrolled in the archer companyof the doughty Sir John Cornwaille, a leader of Henry V\'s army. The army was superb, but sickness and the unexpected French defiance at Harfleur, reduce it to near-shambolic condition. Henry stubbornly refuses to accept defeat and, in appalling weather, leads his shrunken force to what appears to be inevitable disaster.\n\nAzincourt culminates in the battle. Seen from several points of view on the English side, but also from the French ranks, the scene is vivid, convincing and compelling. Bernard Cornwell has a great understanding of men at war and battlefields and this is his masterpiece.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/119121.Conn_Iggulden">About Conn Iggulden</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/119121.Conn_Iggulden"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1235073163p3/119121.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11286314575472714157"><i>Also publishes under author name <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16155974.C_F__Iggulden' title='C.F. Iggulden' rel='nofollow noopener'>C.F. Iggulden</a>.</i><br/><br/>I was born in the normal way in 1971, and vaguely remember half-pennies and sixpences. I have written for as long as I can remember: poetry, short stories and novels. It’s what I always wanted to do and read English at London University with writing in mind. I taught English for seven years and was Head of English at St. Gregory’s RC High School in Lo</span>
  <span id="freeText11286314575472714157" style="display:none"><i>Also publishes under author name <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/16155974.C_F__Iggulden" title="C.F. Iggulden" rel="nofollow noopener">C.F. Iggulden</a>.</i><br /><br />I was born in the normal way in 1971, and vaguely remember half-pennies and sixpences. I have written for as long as I can remember: poetry, short stories and novels. It’s what I always wanted to do and read English at London University with writing in mind. I taught English for seven years and was Head of English at St. Gregory’s RC High School in London by the end of that period. I have enormous respect for those who still labour at the chalk-face. In truth, I can’t find it in me to miss the grind of paperwork and initiatives. I do miss the camaraderie of the smokers’ room, as well as the lessons where their faces lit up as they understood what I was wittering on about.<br /><br />My mother is Irish and from an early age she told me history as an exciting series of stories – with dates. My great-grandfather was a Seannachie, so I suppose story-telling is in the genes somewhere. My father flew in Bomber Command in WWII, then taught maths and science. Perhaps crucially, he also loved poetry and cracking good tales. Though it seems a dated idea now, I began teaching when boys were told only girls were good at English, despite the great names that must spring to mind after that statement. My father loved working with wood and equations, but he also recited ‘Vitai Lampada’ with a gleam in his eye and that matters, frankly.<br /><br />I’ve always loved historical fiction as a genre and cut my teeth on Hornblower and Tai-Pan, Flashman, Sharpe and Jack Aubrey. I still remember the sheer joy of reading my first Patrick O’Brian book and discovering there were nineteen more in the series. I love just about anything by David Gemmell, or Peter F. Hamilton or Wilbur Smith. I suppose the one thing that links all those is the love of a good tale.<br /><br />That’s about it for the moment. If you’d like to get in touch with me leave a comment in the forum or you can tweet me @Conn_Iggulden. I’ll leave it there for the moment. If you’ve read my books, you know an awful lot about the way I think already. There’s no point overdoing it.<br /><br />Conn Iggulden<br /></span>

Temujin\'s young life was shaped by a series of brutal acts: the betrayal of his f<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText16357130305130376959\" style=\"display:none\">From the author of the bestselling &quot;The Dangerous Book for Boys&quot; He was born Temujin, the son of a khan, raised in a clan of hunters migrating across the rugged steppe. Temujin\'s young life was shaped by a series of brutal acts: the betrayal of his father by a neighboring tribe and the abandonment of his entire family, cruelly left to die on the harsh plain. But Temujin endured--and from that moment on, he was driven by a singular fury: to survive in the face of death, to kill before being killed, and to conquer enemies who could come without warning from beyond the horizon.  Through a series of courageous raids against the Tartars, Temujin\'s legend grew. And so did the challenges he faced--from the machinations of a Chinese ambassador to the brutal abduction of his young wife, Borte. Blessed with ferocious courage, it was the young warrior\'s ability to learn, to imagine, and to judge the hearts of others that propelled him to greater and greater power. Until Temujin was chasing a vision: to unite many tribes into one, to make the earth tremble under the hoofbeats of a thousand warhorses, to subject unknown nations and even empires to his will.           $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_7983832').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_7983832').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_7983832').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
